        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsami.2c23236"><meta property="og:title" content="Unprecedented Cyclability and Moisture Durability of NaCrO2 Sodium-Ion Battery Cathode via Simultaneous Al Doping and Cr2O3 Coating"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.2c23236/asset/images/acsami.2c23236.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="Although there are many cathode candidates for sodium-ion batteries (NIBs), NaCrO2 remains one of the most attractive materials due to its reasonable level of capacity, nearly flat reversible voltages, and high thermal stability. However, the cyclic stability of NaCrO2 needs to be further improved in order to compete with other state-of-the-art NIB cathodes. In this study, we show that Cr2O3-coated and Al-doped NaCrO2, which is synthesized through a simple one-pot synthesis, can achieve unprecedented cyclic stability. We confirm the preferential formation of a Cr2O3 shell and a Na(Cr1–2xAl2x)O2 core, rather than xAl2O3/NaCrO2 or Na1/1+2x(Cr1/1+2xAl2x/1+2x)O2, through spectroscopic and microscopic methods. The core/shell compounds exhibit superior electrochemical properties compared to either Cr2O3-coated NaCrO2 without Al dopants or Al-doped NaCrO2 without shells because of their synergistic contributions. As a result, Na(Cr0.98Al0.02)O2 with a thin Cr2O3 layer (5 nm) shows no capacity fading during 1000 charge/discharge cycles while maintaining the rate capability of pristine NaCrO2. In addition, the compound is inert against humid air and water. We also discuss the reasons for the excellent performance of Cr2O3-coated Na(Cr1–2xAl2x)O2."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.2c23236/asset/images/acsami.2c23236.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/1122814~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="931882a2cc5854b8-MAN"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="931882a2cc5854b8-MAN">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: 'c7d55431-b846-44af-acb9-38c5496ee361'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="931882a2cc5854b8-MAN">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'applied_materials_interfaces';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

<script nonce="931882a2cc5854b8-MAN">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "aamick";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Unprecedented Cyclability and Moisture Durability of NaCrO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Sodium-Ion Battery Cathode via Simultaneous Al Doping and Cr&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Coating", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.2c23236", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Unprecedented Cyclability and Moisture Durability of NaCrO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Sodium-Ion Battery Cathode via Simultaneous Al Doping and Cr&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Coating", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.2c23236", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Unprecedented Cyclability and Moisture Durability of NaCrO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Sodium-Ion Battery Cathode via Simultaneous Al Doping and Cr&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Coating", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.2c23236", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Unprecedented Cyclability and Moisture Durability of NaCrO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Sodium-Ion Battery Cathode via Simultaneous Al Doping and Cr&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Coating", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.2c23236", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Unprecedented Cyclability and Moisture Durability of NaCrO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Sodium-Ion Battery Cathode via Simultaneous Al Doping and Cr&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Coating", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.2c23236", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Unprecedented Cyclability and Moisture Durability of NaCrO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Sodium-Ion Battery Cathode via Simultaneous Al Doping and Cr&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Coating", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.2c23236", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Unprecedented Cyclability and Moisture Durability of NaCrO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Sodium-Ion Battery Cathode via Simultaneous Al Doping and Cr&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Coating", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.2c23236", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Unprecedented Cyclability and Moisture Durability of NaCrO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Sodium-Ion Battery Cathode via Simultaneous Al Doping and Cr&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Coating", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.2c23236", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Unprecedented Cyclability and Moisture Durability of NaCrO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Sodium-Ion Battery Cathode via Simultaneous Al Doping and Cr&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;O&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Coating", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.2c23236", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});

class="articleMetrics_count"><h2>Citations</h2><div class="articleMetrics-val"><a href="#citeThis" class="internalNav">3</a></div></div></div></div><div class="articleMetrics_about"><div class="base dropBlock"><a href="#" data-db-target-for="aboutArticleMetrics" aria-describedby="about-article-metrics" class="article_aboutLink">Learn about these metrics</a><div data-db-target-of="aboutArticleMetrics" id="about-article-metrics" class="dropBlock__holder"><button class="articleMetrics_close"> <i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-close_thin"></i><span class="sr-only">close</span></button><p>Article Views are the COUNTER-compliant sum of full text article downloads since November 2008 (both PDF and HTML) across all institutions and individuals. These metrics are regularly updated to reflect usage leading up to the last few days.</p><p>Citations are the number of other articles citing this article, calculated by Crossref and updated daily.<a href="https://www.crossref.org/services/cited-by/"> Find more information about Crossref citation counts.</a></p><p>The Altmetric Attention Score is a quantitative measure of the attention that a research article has received online. Clicking on the donut icon will load a page at altmetric.com with additional details about the score and the social media presence for the given article. Find more information on<a href="https://help.altmetric.com/support/solutions/articles/6000233311-how-is-the-altmetric-attention-score-calculated"> the Altmetric Attention Score and how the score is calculated.</a></p></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.2c23236/asset/images/medium/am2c23236_0008.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.2c23236/asset/images/large/am2c23236_0008.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.2c23236&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">Although there are many cathode candidates for sodium-ion batteries (NIBs), NaCrO<sub>2</sub> remains one of the most attractive materials due to its reasonable level of capacity, nearly flat reversible voltages, and high thermal stability. However, the cyclic stability of NaCrO<sub>2</sub> needs to be further improved in order to compete with other state-of-the-art NIB cathodes. In this study, we show that Cr<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>-coated and Al-doped NaCrO<sub>2</sub>, which is synthesized through a simple one-pot synthesis, can achieve unprecedented cyclic stability. We confirm the preferential formation of a Cr<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> shell and a Na(Cr<sub>1–2<i>x</i></sub>Al<sub>2<i>x</i></sub>)O<sub>2</sub> core, rather than <i>x</i>Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/NaCrO<sub>2</sub> or Na<sub>1/1+2<i>x</i></sub>(Cr<sub>1/1+2<i>x</i></sub>Al<sub>2<i>x</i>/1+2<i>x</i></sub>)O<sub>2</sub>, through spectroscopic and microscopic methods. The core/shell compounds exhibit superior electrochemical properties compared to either Cr<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>-coated NaCrO<sub>2</sub> without Al dopants or Al-doped NaCrO<sub>2</sub> without shells because of their synergistic contributions. As a result, Na(Cr<sub>0.98</sub>Al<sub>0.02</sub>)O<sub>2</sub> with a thin Cr<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> layer (5 nm) shows no capacity fading during 1000 charge/discharge cycles while maintaining the rate capability of pristine NaCrO<sub>2</sub>. In addition, the compound is inert against humid air and water. We also discuss the reasons for the excellent performance of Cr<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>-coated Na(Cr<sub>1–2<i>x</i></sub>Al<sub>2<i>x</i></sub>)O<sub>2</sub>.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.

                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Na-ion+Battery&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_Na-ion%20battery">Na-ion battery</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Nacro2&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_NaCrO2">NaCrO<sub>2</sub></a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Core%E2%88%92shell&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_core%E2%88%92shell">core−shell</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Al+Doping&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_Al%20doping">Al doping</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Cr2o3&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_Cr2O3">Cr<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub></a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">Due to the anticipated future shortage of lithium, there has been extensive research on room-temperature sodium-ion batteries (NIBs) over the past few decades as a potential alternative to the market-dominating lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), particularly for large-scale energy storage systems. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref1" aria-label="reference 1">(1)</a> Despite continuous technological improvements, the overall performance of NIBs still lags behind LIBs, although certain properties of battery components have become comparable to those used in state-of-the-art LIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref2" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref2" aria-label="reference 2">(2)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">In terms of cathode materials, polyanion-type compounds <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref3" aria-label="reference 3">(3)</a> and layered transition-metal oxides <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref4" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref4" aria-label="reference 4">(4)</a> are two representative examples that have undergone numerous modifications in terms of elemental compositions, crystallographic structures, and particle morphologies. Polyanion-type compounds (e.g., phosphates, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref5" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref5" aria-label="reference 5">(5)</a> pyrophosphates, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref6" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref6" aria-label="reference 6">(6)</a> fluorophosphates, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref7" aria-label="reference 7">(7)</a> NASICON structures, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref8" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref8" aria-label="reference 8">(8)</a> sulfates, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref9" aria-label="reference 9">(9)</a> and silicates <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref10" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref10" aria-label="reference 10">(10)</a>) are generally composed of tetrahedron anionic units interconnected with transition-metal polyhedral units, which contribute to high operating potential and cyclic stability. However, the relatively low electronic conductivity of polyanion-type cathodes often compromises these advantageous features, leading to insufficient rate capabilities, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref11" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref11" aria-label="reference 11">(11)</a> unless surface or morphological modifications are made. On the other hand, relatively high electronic/ionic conductivities of layered transition-metal oxides enable fast charge/discharge (C/D), but multiple phase transitions during C/D often degrade the cyclability. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref4 ref12" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref4 ref12" aria-label="reference 4 and 12">(4,12)</a> Humidity sensitivity also complicates electrode fabrication and/or long-term storage. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref13" aria-label="reference 13">(13)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">O3-NaCrO<sub>2</sub> is a highly promising cathode material in the class of layered transition-metal oxides due to its reversible capacity, almost constant C/D voltages, and excellent thermal stability. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14 ref15" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref14 ref15" aria-label="reference 14 and 15">(14,15)</a> However, O3-NaCrO<sub>2</sub> undergoes multiple phase transitions during C/D. It reversibly transforms to O3/O′3, O′3, O′3/P′3, and P′3 with Na<sup>+</sup> extraction up to Na<sub>0.4–0.5</sub>CrO<sub>2</sub>, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref16" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref16" aria-label="reference 16">(16)</a> and further removal of Na<sup>+</sup> results in irreversible structure changes from layered to rocksalt through disproportionation/comproportionation with concomitant migration of chromium ions. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref17" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref17" aria-label="reference 17">(17)</a> However, although the degree of desodiation is restricted to Na<sub>0.5</sub>CrO<sub>2</sub> for better cyclability, the capacity continuously decreases with repeated C/D. Pristine O3-NaCrO<sub>2</sub> commonly shows capacity retention less than 80% of initial capacities within 100 C/D cycles. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14 ref18 ref19" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref14 ref18 ref19" aria-label="reference 14, 18 and 19">(14,18,19)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">To address the stability issue of O3-NaCrO<sub>2</sub>, the control of phase transitions and thus the mitigation of dimensional changes have been investigated through isovalent/aliovalent substitution for Cr<sup>3+</sup>. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20 ref21 ref22 ref23 ref24 ref25 ref26" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref20 ref21 ref22 ref23 ref24 ref25 ref26" aria-label="reference 20 to 26">(20−26)</a> For example, Ma et al. recently reported that phase transitions can occur through an O3/P3 solid–solution state with no O′3 monoclinic phase by Sb substitutions. O3–Na<sub>0.9</sub>Cr<sub>0.9</sub>Sb<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> retained 70.9% of its initial capacity (111 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>) after 1000 C/D cycles compared to 46.8% retention in pristine NaCrO<sub>2</sub>. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref25" aria-label="reference 25">(25)</a> Surface modification has also been investigated to improve cyclic stability, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18 ref19 ref27 ref28 ref29" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref18 ref19 ref27 ref28 ref29" aria-label="reference 18, 19 and 27 to 29">(18,19,27−29)</a> in which the surface layer either suppresses side reactions on the cathode surface (e.g., oxidation of chemical species reduced on anodes) or prevents solvent insertion into Na layers. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14 ref30" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref14 ref30" aria-label="reference 14 and 30">(14,30)</a> Carbon was the most popular choice in this category, and various precursors, including citric acid, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref18" aria-label="reference 18">(18)</a> pitch, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref19" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref19" aria-label="reference 19">(19)</a> coffee waste, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref24" aria-label="reference 24">(24)</a> and acetylene, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref25" aria-label="reference 25">(25)</a> have been used for the carbon coating of O3-NaCrO<sub>2</sub>. Among them, pitch-derived carbon-coated O3-NaCrO<sub>2</sub> showed the highest cyclic stability, with approximately 90% of its initial capacity retained after 300 C/D cycles. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref19" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref19" aria-label="reference 19">(19)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">Oxide coating, which is a common approach in other cathode materials, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref31 ref32" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref31 ref32" aria-label="reference 31 and 32">(31,32)</a> has been rarely explored in O3-NaCrO<sub>2</sub>. However, a recent study by Wang et al. showed the positive effect of in-situ-generated Cr<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> layers on the cyclic stability of O3-NaCrO<sub>2</sub>. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref29" aria-label="reference 29">(29)</a> The capacity retention of Cr<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>-coated NaCrO<sub>2</sub> was greatly improved in NaClO<sub>4</sub>/propylene carbonate electrolytes containing fluorinated ethylene carbonate (FEC) additives (83.8% capacity retention after 300 cycles at 120 mA g<sup>–1</sup>).</div><div class="NLM_p">In this work, we present the one-pot synthesis of <i>x</i>Cr<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>-coated Na(Cr<sub>1–2<i>x</i></sub>Al<sub>2<i>x</i></sub>)O<sub>2</sub> and its remarkable cyclability in additive-free electrolytes. While numerous studies have investigated bulk doping or surface coating in other types of layered materials, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref33 ref34 ref35 ref36" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref33 ref34 ref35 ref36" aria-label="reference 33 to 36">(33−36)</a> this is the first report on simultaneous doping and coating in NaCrO<sub>2</sub>. Through spectroscopic and microscopic analyses, we demonstrate that the phase separation of Cr<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/Al-doped NaCrO<sub>2</sub> is preferred over the formation of Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/NaCrO<sub>2</sub> or Na-deficient Na<sub>1–2<i>x</i></sub>Cr<sub>1–2<i>x</i></sub>Al<sub>2<i>x</i></sub>O<sub>2</sub>. By combining surface modification and isovalent doping, we show that <i>x</i>Cr<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>-coated Na(Cr<sub>1–2<i>x</i></sub>Al<sub>2<i>x</i></sub>)O<sub>2</sub> exhibits unparalleled cyclic stability (<a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">Table 1</a>), <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14 ref18 ref19 ref20 ref21 ref22 ref23 ref24 ref25 ref26 ref27 ref28 ref29 ref37 ref38" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref14 ref18 ref19 ref20 ref21 ref22 ref23 ref24 ref25 ref26 ref27 ref28 ref29 ref37 ref38" aria-label="reference 14, 18 to 29, 37 and 38">(14,18−29,37,38)</a> which cannot be achieved solely by either Cr<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> coating or Al doping. We investigate the significant improvement in cyclability through synchrotron-based in-situ XRD patterns and changes in chromium concentrations in the electrolyte solution. Furthermore, we show that <i>x</i>Cr<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>-coated Na(Cr<sub>1–2<i>x</i></sub>Al<sub>2<i>x</i></sub>)O<sub>2</sub> is perfectly inert in humid air and even in water, providing an additional benefit. Our findings expand the range of potential cathode candidates and contribute to the commercialization of NIBs.</div><div class="NLM_table-wrap" id="tbl1"><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption"><div class="NLM_caption" id=""><div class="title2">Table 1. 0.5C</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">136, 50</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">–0.403</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">charged-3.8 V</td><td class="colsep0 class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">Na<sub>0.90</sub>(Cr<sub>0.95</sub>Sb<sub>0.05</sub>)O<sub>2</sub></td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">114 @ 5.0C</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">80.8, 1000</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">–0.033</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">&nbsp;</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left"> <a align="left">Na<sub>0.94</sub>(Cr<sub>0.97</sub>Nb<sub>0.03</sub>)O<sub>2</sub></td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">119 @ 0.1C</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">113, 35</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">–0.171</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">&nbsp;</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left"> <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26"
